Lowers the AST to the HIR.\n//!\n//! Since the AST and HIR are fairly similar, this is mostly a simple procedure,\n//! much like a fold. Where lowering involves a bit more work things get more\n//! interesting and there are some invariants you should know about. These mostly\n//! concern spans and IDs.\n//!\n//! Spans are assigned to AST nodes during parsing and then are modified during\n//! expansion to indicate the origin of a node and the process it went through\n//! being expanded. IDs are assigned to AST nodes just before lowering.\n//!\n//! For the simpler lowering steps, IDs and spans should be preserved. Unlike\n//! expansion we do not preserve the process of lowering in the spans, so spans\n//! should not be modified here. When creating a new node (as opposed to\n//! \"folding\" an existing one), create a new ID using `next_id()`.\n//!\n//! You must ensure that IDs are unique. That means that you should only use the\n//! ID from an AST node in a single HIR node (you can assume that AST node-IDs\n//! are unique). Every new node must have a unique ID. Avoid cloning HIR nodes.\n//! If you do, you must then set the new node's ID to a fresh one.\n//!\n//! Spans are used for error messages and for tools to map semantics back to\n//! source code. It is therefore not as important with spans as IDs to be strict\n//! about use (you can't break the compiler by screwing up a span). Obviously, a\n//! HIR node can only have a single span. But multiple nodes can have the same\n//! span and spans don't need to be kept in order, etc. Where code is preserved\n//! by lowering, it should have the same span as in the AST. Where HIR nodes are\n//! new it is probably best to give a span for the whole AST node being lowered.\n//! All nodes should have real spans; don't use dummy spans. dummy_syn_ext(guar.unwrap());\n            };\n            let args = mbe::macro_parser::compute_locs(&delimited.tts);\n            let body_span = lhs_span;\n            rules.push(MacroRule::Attr { unsafe_rule, args, args_span, body: lhs, body_span, rhs });\n        } else if is_derive {\n            rules.push(MacroRule::Derive { body: lhs, body_span: lhs_span, rhs });\n        } else {\n            rules.push(MacroRule::Func { lhs, lhs_span, rhs });\n        }\n        if p.token == token::Eof {\n            break;\n        }\n        if let Err(e) = p.expect(exp_sep) {\n            return dummy_syn_ext(e.emit());\n        }\n    }\n\n    if rules.is_empty() {\n        let guar = sess.dcx().span_err(span, \"macros must contain at least one rule\");\n        return dummy_syn_ext(guar);\n fn transcribe<'a>(\n    psess: &'a ParseSess,\n    interp: &FxHashMap<MacroRulesNormalizedIdent, NamedMatch>,\n    src: &mbe::Delimited,\n    src_span: DelimSpan,\n    transparency: Transparency,\n TranscrCtx {\n        psess,\n        interp,\n        marker: Marker { expand_id, transparency, cache: Default::default() },\n        repeats: Vec::new(),\n        stack: smallvec![Frame::new_delimited(\n            src,\n            src_span,\n            DelimSpacing::new(Spacing::Alone, Spacing::Alone)\n        )],\n        result: Vec::new(),\n        result_stack: Vec::new(),\n    };\n\n    loop {\n        // Look at the last frame on the stack.\n        // If it still has a TokenTree we have not looked at yet, use that tree.\n        let Some(tree) = end of a sequence and we can keep repeating,\n            // go back to the beginning of the sequence.\n            let frame = tscx.stack.last_mut().unwrap();\n            if let FrameKind::Sequence { sep, .. } = &frame.kind {\n                let (repeat_idx, repeat_len) = tscx.repeats.last_mut().unwrap();\n                *repeat_idx += 1;\n                if repeat_idx < repeat_len {\n                    frame.idx = 0;\n                    if let Some(sep) = sep {\n                        tscx.result.push(TokenTree::Token(*sep, Spacing::Alone));\n                    }\n                    continue;\n                }\n            }\n\n            // We are done with the top of the stack. Pop it. Depending on what it was, we do\n            // different things. Note that the outermost item must be the delimited, wrapped RHS\n            // that was passed in originally to `transcribe`.\n            match tscx.stack.pop().unwrap().kind {\n                // Done with a sequence. Pop from repeats.\n                FrameKind::Sequence { .. } => {\n                    tscx.repeats.pop();\n                }\n\n                // We are done processing a Delimited. If this is the top-level delimited, we are\n                // done. Otherwise, we unwind the result_stack to append what we have produced to\n                // any previous results.\n                FrameKind::Delimited { delim, span, mut spacing, .. } => {\n                    // Hack to force-insert a space after `]` in certain case.\n                    // See discussion of the `hex-literal` crate in #114571.\n                    if delim == Delimiter::Bracket {\n                        spacing.close = Spacing::Alone;\n                    }\n                    if tscx.result_stack.is_empty() {\n                        // No results left to compute! &mbe::TokenTree::MetaVar(sp, original_ident) => {\n                transcribe_metavar(&mut tscx, sp, original_ident)?;\n            }\n\n            // Replace meta-variable expressions with the
